He mentions his house many times, which he refers to by the Anglo-French "desmesne" most of the time. Throughout, the notes mention times when he had to provide favors owed from when he claimed the house, and details (quite bitterly) what resources were spent. They're phrased in terms of either time spent, power granted for some purpose, or in gibberish-like names. They're always granted to abbreviations, not to full names. Example: "broke another shell of the Opener in exchange for A.W.'s aid. One left." followed by scratchings of "hate him" or "Sent the shambler to M.T., debt paid"
He talks about his "immortality". Not how he achieved it, but of its tragedy. He rambles about the neighborhood no longer providing enough "fortune" to feed his spells and curses "Thomas" for it. He seems to be overtaken by madness, many of the notes being incoherent scratches or scribbles for periods of time.
He talks about his athame, the ritual dagger. He talks about sporadic sacrifices; cats, rats, and attempted human sacrifices to lift himself from his fugue. Even with his athame supposedly "streamlining the transfer of blood to power", it's never enough.
Carmen Santamonica eyes the dagger warily
And throughout, he talks more and more about the rats. He workshops a way to use a medallion he procured to funnel "the whispers of Khnum", which allowed him to control rats, bugs, and other vermin. He complains about its lack of finesse, but there's enough here to detail how to enact this yourself if you have the dagger and medallion.

Luck is unique. Luck is used both for determining targets for monsters (sometimes) and for determining things that you don't really have any control over.
You can find the stat under the normal stats, to the far right
Any time you make a roll, you can permanently reduce your LUCK by an amount to improve your roll by that much. This can turn a failure into a success
As an alternative, any non-combat roll can be Pushed. If you Push a roll then you get a free reroll! However, if you fail a Pushed roll, then it counts as a Complication, which I can use to make bad things happen to you.

The house itself is silent, shuttered, and brooding. Cobwebbed by ivy, masked by trees, and caressed by the wind. It is large and apparently well-constructed, with high ceilings and thick, substantial windows, walls, and doors. From the outside, the entire edifice presents a strange, slightly skewed or tilted appearance. The foundations seem solid enough when viewed closely, but the house itself seems a little... crooked.

GM: Just a quick announcement here: I got some feedback from y'all, and I want to adjust how we do our exploration and fact-finding.
IllymetWaltsy (Carmen Santamonica): WELL, I think we DID decide on that first thing, I don't remember if there was a consensu on the second part
GM: One common point is that there's a bit of difficulty with order of actions and with more tension. So to address those I want to implement Turns, similar to OD&D
IllymetWaltsy (Carmen Santamonica): Yeah okay that would make sense!
GM: One Turn is 30min, and allows you to do a thorough search. You can do a sped up search in 15min if you accept +1P (one penalty die) for your roll. Spending a Turn looking things over suggests a more thorough investigation than just glancing around.
GM: This will both ensure that all four players are able to do something (rather than one player getting accidentally steamrolled) and also put a bit of a cost on your searches
Ayji (Lillian Lovell): that makes sense
GM: You could all spend a Turn searching Cornthwaite's room, but that means we go from 4:00pm to 4:30pm. If you all fail, you can do it again, but then it goes from 4:30pm to 5:00pm
GM: This should also encourage splitting up, since reasonably you don't need four of you doing a search in one room to expect at least one success
IllymetWaltsy (Carmen Santamonica): ...With how we roll?
GM: Though if you want to, you absolutely can, it'll just take twice as long
IllymetWaltsy (Carmen Santamonica): Either or would be fine with me based on GM feeling for the situation
GM: If you have two or more people searching a room, you can split the work up to make it go faster. One person checks one half, and the other person checks the other half, and it takes half as long. BUT, if someone misses their roll on the upper half, y'all may miss information that is hidden their (ie the secret fireplace)
IllymetWaltsy (Carmen Santamonica): This is making logical sense and helping to bridge the dice and real world. I like it!
Ayji (Lillian Lovell): I'm not carmen is
